National Federation of Commerce Calls for Implementation of Resolutions from the People's Food Conference 173

Appeal from Businessmen and Residents of Dangtu County, Anhui Province

The National Federation of Commerce yesterday telegraphed the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Supervisory Yuan, and the Ministry of Finance, stating: "We have received an urgent telegram from the Chamber of Commerce of Dangtu County, Anhui Province, stating that this year's grain prices have plummeted, the rural economy is bankrupt, and there is already the danger of farmers abandoning their fields. However, the authorities in Anhui not only fail to show compassion or provide relief, but instead impose heavy taxes on the only lifeline of rice and grain, making it impossible to turn the low prices into money. This is directly driving 30 million people to disaster. The enemy's intentions are realized, and our worries are endless. In addition to sending telegrams to appeal, we earnestly request your federation to intervene and alleviate this dire situation." We have received this communication. Upon investigation, the drop in grain prices has already led to the bankruptcy of the rural economy. The central government previously convened a National People's Food Conference, and the first resolution was to ensure the unobstructed flow of food within the country. Now, after the National People's Food Conference, the Anhui Provincial Government has resumed levying taxes on exported rice and grain, with each dan taxed as high as sixty cents, which is completely contrary to the purpose of the central government's convening of the Food Conference. We hereby submit this to your departments and yuan for review and approval, earnestly requesting that the Anhui Provincial Government be promptly ordered to stop this practice to alleviate the suffering of the people, and to quickly implement all resolutions of the People's Food Conference. This is our most sincere plea. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, respectfully.

Jiangbei Reclamation Inspection Group Departs Yesterday Morning 174

He Yushu to Inspect Site for Opening Port at Haizhou

The Jiangbei Reclamation Inspection Group organized by the Jiangsu Provincial Government departed at 2:00 AM this morning on the Daqing ship, first heading to Nantong. Group members He Yushu, Miao Bin, Pi Zuoqiong, Chen Zhen, Zhang Pengzhou, and several others boarded the ship last night. After inspecting Nantong, they will proceed to Haizhou by sea, as He and others are also tasked with surveying the site for opening a port at Xugou, Haizhou. After completing inspections in the Haizhou area, they will transfer to Xuzhou and take the Tianjin-Pukou Railway southward back to Suzhou.

Outline of the Comprehensive Shanghai Gazetteer Finalized by the Shanghai Municipal Gazetteer Office 175

Since Mr. Liu Yazi and Mr. Zhu Shaoping took office at the Shanghai Municipal Gazetteer Office, they have immediately engaged in organization, hiring editorial staff, and actively proceeding with the work. The categories and general outline of the comprehensive gazetteer were finalized early on, and editing has already begun. We have now obtained the tentative categories and general outline of the Shanghai Municipal Gazetteer from the office and are publishing them below, which we believe will be welcomed by those concerned. Before the categories and general outline, there are several "Remarks to Readers," which are also included below:

Remarks to Readers 1. The members of the editorial department of this office, with reference to local gazetteers from various parts of our country and various foreign annual reports, and based on the actual situation in Shanghai, have divided the Shanghai Municipal Gazetteer into twenty-five categories on a tentative basis. The organizational methods of these twenty-five categories can be roughly divided into four parts: (1) Categories 1 to 5 describe Shanghai's history and geography and its general situation, belonging to the nature of a general overview in the overall organization of the gazetteer. (2) Categories 6 to 13 focus on describing the various administrative conditions of Shanghai throughout history, belonging to the nature of the main body in the overall organization of the gazetteer. (3) Categories 14 to 22 describe the various aspects of the situation of the people of Shanghai, also belonging to the nature of the main body in the overall organization of the gazetteer. (4) Categories 23 to 25 are charts and graphs for reference when reading the various categories of this gazetteer, belonging to the nature of a conclusion in the overall organization of the gazetteer. 2. The general outline of the twenty-five categories of the gazetteer is tentatively based on the tentative categories and has not been reviewed by specialists. Inadequacies are certainly unavoidable and will be revised. Furthermore, if historical materials are abundant during editing, they will be expanded and changed. 3. The content of each category of the gazetteer may have overlaps with each other. Except for necessary ones, the editorial staff of this office will gather together and often discuss them to strive to avoid them. 4. Below the general outline, there are sub-items. For example, the general outline of the Finance Category has only seven items, but the sub-items total twenty-two. Detailed sub-items for all categories will be printed separately later and then requested for further instruction. 5. Domestic scholars are earnestly hoped to provide practical criticisms of the tentative categories and general outline of this office in order to correct any shortcomings. 6. Although the categories, general outline, and sub-items of this gazetteer have all been tentatively determined, there are still many difficulties in editing, in addition to collecting various historical materials. For example, the former of the two categories of customs and local conditions and figures suffers from being tedious and trivial, and the latter lacks standards. If various circles can give us their insightful opinions, our colleagues will accept them sincerely. Attached notice 1. Due to the limited human resources and finances of our office, we can only realistically work on what is permitted by the current facts and proceed step by step. As for various large-scale plans, we dare not make any predictions at this time. 2. Our office's reference books and reference materials are extremely scarce. We hope that those who sympathize with our office will do their best to help, either by donating books, photos, or newspapers, or by transcribing historical materials. We will be extremely grateful for everything. 3. We hope that those who receive the various survey forms issued by our office will be happy to fill them out and return them to our office. 4. Many people in Shanghai still fail to understand the nature of a gazetteer. We hope that those who sympathize with our office can clarify it anytime and anywhere so that we can proceed without error.

Xu Shiying's Reply to Quan Shaowu's Telegram 176

Regarding the case of the dispute over disaster relief in northern Anhui, the Anhui Native Place Association of this port previously filed a complaint in the name of its standing committee. The plaintiff's agent included Mr. Xu Shiying's name. Mr. Xu believed that he was a member of the Flood Relief Association, and credit and blame should be shared, so he could not be an agent for the litigation. He immediately entrusted lawyer Li Shirui to withdraw his name from the case at the court. Later, a newspaper reported the news and still listed Mr. Xu's name. At that time, Xu had returned to his hometown for mourning. After hearing about it, he formally published a notice in the newspaper to clarify the matter, and the Shanghai Anhui Native Place Association sent a letter to make corrections. Recently, Xu and Cha Mianzhong and Quan Shaowu exchanged telegrams, and many newspapers have published them. The reply to Mr. Quan is recorded below: "To Brother Quan Shaowu, care of Zhu Yulao in Beiping: I received your telegram. There is no brother's name in the court's accusation. It is a pity for you to issue such absurd words based only on erroneous newspapers. I am the chairman of the Central Disaster Relief Committee and also a member of the National Government Relief Committee. Credit and blame should be shared. If I know that you have done wrong, I will report it to Chairman Song for investigation. There is no need for me to file a lawsuit in my personal name. The Shanghai newspaper has made corrections, which you may not know. The details are in the reply to Brother Zhongmian. Please read it. I have not heard about the lawsuit. Heaven can bear witness. If you must engage in legal proceedings, I will see you after the seven weeks of mourning for my father are over. Ying Yan."

Swire Shipping Company Decides to Postpone Implementation of New Standards 177

Social Bureau Schedules Signing

After the Swire Shipping Company, a British company, stipulated the standards for mid-cabin workers on the Yangtze River route, a labor-management dispute arose. The Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Industry all instructed the Municipal Government to handle the matter properly. After the Social Bureau repeatedly tried to mediate, a conclusion is now within sight. The details are as follows:

Postponed Implementation The Swire Yangtze River route, including nine ships such as the Anqing, would inevitably have to lay off more than 1,000 people according to the newly stipulated standards. After mediation by the Municipal Social Bureau and the Municipal Party Headquarters, the company's manager initially had a very tough attitude, insisting that it must be implemented. He had notified the compradors of each ship to stay in Shanghai to handle the matter. Now that he deeply knows that it is not easy to do so in reality, he has recently notified the compradors of each ship that the five measures stipulated by the company will be postponed. As a result, the compradors of each ship stopped staying in Shanghai and sailed with the ships.

Scheduled Signing In order to eliminate future disturbances, all mid-cabin workers requested that a specific method be decided. The Social Bureau proposed three principles, which were approved by the China Shipping Mutual Aid Association and the Seamen's Mid-Cabin Guild. The bureau has now scheduled a meeting for 2:00 PM on November 10th to reconvene representatives from the Seamen's Mid-Cabin Guild and the China Shipping Mutual Aid Association to formally sign and resolve the matter.

The Ministry Appoints Wen Yuqing as Successor

New Director to Take Office on the 11th After Zhu Jiahao became the Minister of Communications, the original Director of the Telegraph Administration and concurrently Director of the International Telegraph Office, Zhong Zhuo, and Lu Cheng jointly requested to resign from their respective positions. Travel Agency徵集 Famous Scenery Photography for the Chicago Exposition Exhibition 180

A Large-Scale Photography Exhibition Will Be Held First in Shanghai

The China Travel Service on Szechuan Road, Shanghai, has been entrusted by the Acquisition Department of the Preparatory Committee for the Republic of China's participation in the Chicago Exposition to徵集 photographs of famous Chinese scenic spots to be displayed in the United States, aiming to showcase our beautiful landscapes and promote our national glory. This undertaking is of great significance. In addition to organizing and enlarging the photographs collected over the years in preparation for shipment to the United States, the company is also publicly徵集 submissions, hoping that various photography groups and experts will actively participate and contribute to this grand event. The company also plans to hold a large-scale photography exhibition in Shanghai after the deadline for submissions, inviting experts to evaluate all entries. The best works will be awarded commemorative gifts. The徵集 guidelines are as follows: ㈠ The company has been entrusted by the Acquisition Department of the Preparatory Committee for China's participation in the Chicago Exposition to徵集 submissions of Chinese scenic photography. ㈡ Submitted photographs must meet one of the following criteria: A. Scenic landscapes from various regions; B. Historical sites of value; C. Modern and beautiful buildings; D. Excellent highway photography from various regions; E. Photography of new municipal facilities in various regions; F. Various works with artistic merit. ㈢ The size of submitted photographs should be 16 inches wide and 20 inches long. ㈣ Submitted photographs must include detailed explanations in Chinese and English on a separate sheet of paper. If English explanations cannot be provided, the Acquisition Department will translate them separately. ㈤ Submitted photographs that cannot be framed must be mounted on thick paper and carefully sealed to prevent damage during shipping. ㈥ Entrants must provide detailed contact addresses for communication purposes. ㈦ Entrants from inland areas who do not have qualified photographers to enlarge their photos can send their negatives to the company for enlargement. If the company deems the negatives unworthy of enlargement, they will be returned (provided that the entrant pays the return postage in advance). ㈧ Submitted photographs must be sent to the Famous Scenery Photography Section of the China Travel Service at 114 Szechuan Road, Shanghai, before December 20, 1932. ㈨ The company plans to hold a public exhibition in Shanghai on February 4, 1933, for the public to appreciate. ㈩ When holding the photography exhibition, the company will invite experts to evaluate the entries. The best works will be sent to the Acquisition Department of the Preparatory Committee for China's participation in the Chicago Exposition for display in the United States, and the company will also award commemorative gifts. ㈩㈠ In addition to the above guidelines, all other matters concerning submissions will be handled in accordance with the regulations of the Preparatory Committee for China's participation in the Chicago Exposition.

A Bizarre Murder Case Occurred at a Writer's Gathering 181

Just Moved into a Room in a Lane House

A Woman Was Strangled to Death That Night

Lu Hou, a 62-year-old landlady from Nanjing, residing at No. 13 Shude Lane, Xujiahui Town, Shanghai, has four sons, all of whom work elsewhere. Her eldest daughter-in-law, Zhang, lives with Hou on the upper floor, while her third daughter-in-law, Li, lives downstairs. Only the three women reside in the house. Recently, the tenant in the lane house room moved out, so a rental advertisement was posted at the entrance. On the morning of the previous day, a man in his thirties, wearing a long blue cloth gown, claiming to be from Jiangyin and a professor at Nanyang University, inquired about renting the lane house room. Li led him to view the room, and they agreed on a monthly rent of four yuan and fifty cents, with one yuan paid in advance. Around 5:00 PM, the tenant arrived with a woman, bringing bedding, a bamboo suitcase, and some scattered items. Around 7:00 PM, Hou went upstairs to collect the rent and inquire about their identities. She saw the two tenants cooking in the room, with nothing unusual. They replied that the rent would be paid the next day. Unexpectedly, the woman was strangled to death that night, and the murderer escaped at 6:00 AM the next morning. It was not until 4:00 PM yesterday that Hou, not seeing the woman come downstairs, went to the lane house room to collect the remaining three yuan and fifty cents in rent. She saw the woman lying covered by a quilt, called out to her but received no response, and pushed her but could not wake her. When she uncovered the quilt, she was horrified to find a strangled female corpse. Hou was shocked and ran to report to the Second Precinct of the Sixth District of the town. The patrol officer was dispatched to investigate and found that the woman, approximately thirty years old, had a hemp rope around her neck, wore a blue cloth jacket, black cloth trousers, and thread socks, resembling a servant. Apart from a bed, there were no other belongings in the room. The case is very bizarre, and it has not been reported to the household registration office, so the surname is unknown. Yesterday, the local security officer Zhang Qinpu was ordered to report to the court for an inspection. Due to the late hour, officials will be dispatched today for examination.

Workers at the French-Owned Water and Electricity Company's Coppersmith Shop Go on Strike 182

Refusal to Grant Holidays

Causes 工人怠工

The entire workforce of over six hundred coppersmiths at the French-owned Water and Electricity Company went on strike yesterday afternoon due to the company's refusal to grant them holidays. Our reporter made specific inquiries to the workers regarding the cause of the strike. According to the workers, on the last day of the annual Grand Racing Carnival, the workers were given a holiday according to precedent, and because today (that is, today) is the last day of the Autumn Racing Carnival, they should not be an exception. When work ended at 11:00 AM today (yesterday), the workers made a request to the authorities but were unexpectedly severely rejected by the foreman. The workers considered the foreman to be violating the precedents and then all went on strike at 1:00 PM. It is said that until 6:00 PM that evening, all six hundred workers left the factory together and went to the labor union to make a resolution. This morning, if there is no key solution, they may have to petition the Municipal Government and the Bureau of Social Affairs.

Anhui People Deny Loan from Anhui Provincial Government 183

The Anhui Fellow-Provincials Association and the Anhui Students Association in Shanghai Telegraphed National Banks to Deny the Anhui Provincial Government's Loan Matters

To the attention of all banks nationwide, as forwarded by the local newspapers: Our province of Anhui has suffered frequent disasters in recent years, and its vitality has been depleted. However, the provincial government authorities have disregarded the people's hardships and have both illegally collected 口照 donations and arbitrarily issued 5 million in road construction bonds, even designating rice donation revenue as collateral. What exploitation can the survivors after the calamity endure? The people of Anhui vow never to recognize this. Therefore, on the first day of this month, a joint meeting of all Anhui public organizations in Shanghai was held, and it was unanimously resolved to notify all banks nationwide that they should not underwrite or mortgage bonds issued by the Anhui provincial government to avoid being implicated. In addition to dispatching representatives to the government to appeal, we hereby send a telegram to the banking industry across the country based on the resolution of the conference, urging that the road construction bonds issued by the Anhui provincial government should not be underwritten or mortgaged. If there is any private transfer of funds, the people of Anhui will absolutely not be responsible for repayment. The examples of Ni Sichong and Ma Lianjia in the past serve as precedents. We respectfully inform you. The Anhui Fellow-Provincials Association and the Anhui Students Association in Shanghai respectfully salute.

The Decline of the Yangtze River National Steamships 184

Lack of Cargo, the Route Along the Yangtze River. After the January 28th Incident this year, domestic financial stagnation, the cessation of trade by visiting merchants, coupled with the year's floods, reduced the purchasing power of the people. Furthermore, the outbreak of the Sichuan War disrupted the arrival of goods from the upper Yangtze River, and imports were also greatly reduced. The sharp decline in goods shipped from Shanghai led to a slump in the business of national steamships on the Yangtze River. Currently, the number of regular Jianglun (Yangtze River steamer) outgoing shipments to the upper reaches is only two to three-tenths of the usual amount. In the past, each round trip would generate freight revenue of around 10,000 yuan, but now it only brings in 2,000 to 3,000 yuan, which is not enough to cover the cost of fuel.

Reduced Ships, The most numerous of the Yangtze River national steamships is the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which has always been considered the backbone of shipping. According to the company's current business report, apart from the Jiangshun and Jiang'an ships, other ships such as Jiangyu, Jiangxin, Jianguo, and Jiangjing are still operating, but due to a shortage of cargo, all ships are reporting losses, with none making a profit. The Sanbei Company originally had eight ships operating on the Yangtze River, but due to the decline in business, three ships have been withdrawn, and the rest have been rerouted to places such as Haizhou to reduce losses. The Ningjing Wheel from the Ning Shao company has also stopped operating. This year's downturn in the Yangtze River shipping industry is rare in decades.

Upper Yangtze River Increases Additional Draft Surcharge 185

With the Water Level in the Upper Yangtze River Rapidly Declining, the Changsha Route has already had its Draft Surcharge Increased by 50% through Discussions by Five Companies. Yesterday, local shipping companies continued to receive telegrams indicating that the river water in Hunan Province was decreasing daily. Therefore, Taikoo and other companies have agreed that starting from the 11th of this month, the waterway transportation fee from Hankou to Changde will be increased by onefold of the original price. From Hankou to Shashi Yichang route it was agreed that, starting from the 26th of this month, the waterway transportation fee will be increased by 25% of the original price. Yesterday, all cargo owners have been notified to follow this instruction.

Zhejiang Boxed Tea Transport to Shanghai Ends 186

Sales Abroad More Developed Than Last Year

This year, the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway transported boxed tea from Zhejiang Province's Quzhou, Yan, and Anhui areas, starting in May. The Huitong Forwarding Company gradually reported and loaded shipments from the Zha Kou station to Shanghai, and a special price contract was agreed upon with the railway bureau. It has been learned that this item of boxed tea has now finished transport. A total of over 182,000 boxes have been delivered to the South Station for unloading, and over 45,000 boxes have been unloaded at the North Station, a total of over 230,000 boxes. This is an increase of over 20,000 boxes compared to last year. Exports and sales of boxed tea abroad this year are also more developed than last year, it is said.

The Taxpayers Association Sends a Letter to the Public Works Department to Take into Account the Difficulties of the Shack Dwellers in Eastern Shanghai 187

A Fundamental Solution Should Be Planned Before Taking Action

Allowing Them to Live Exposed to Snow and Frost is Contrary to Humanity

The Chinese Taxpayers Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Director-General of the Public Works Department yesterday, stating: "We are writing to you concerning a letter from the Shanghai East Shack Dwellers' Delegation stating that the shack dwellers along the Yangshupu roads are all famine refugees and manual laborers. Recently, the Public Works Department of the Public Concession suddenly issued notices, using the excuse of unregistered residence to forcibly demolish their homes. We have heard that this is due to the request of a small number of landlords whose houses have been neglected due to the Shanghai Incident. Moreover, registered livestock pens, such as pigsties and furniture, are also being destroyed. We have learned that these shack dwellers are both ignorant of the law and lack financial resources, and their livelihoods have been cut off, causing them great consternation. We are writing to request that you immediately submit this matter to the council, and that enforcement should not continue until the case is resolved. Furthermore, you should order your subordinates to protect those who have registered, provide guarantees to those who have registered, grant special permission for remedies to those who have not registered, and restore the demolished areas to their original state in order to maintain the livelihood of the people. We would be deeply grateful for your consideration." The representatives also personally described their suffering to the association. We have learned that unregistered shacks are indeed a violation of established regulations. However, after the Japanese army disturbed Shanghai, cheap housing was reduced to ashes, and existing businesses were unable to sustain themselves. Seeking to eke out a living, they were forced to take this step. We should overlook the circumstances and show leniency. According to the delegation, they heard that this was done at the request of the landlords. The association is confident that this is not the case. Building affordable public housing for rent would be a fundamental solution to the problem of shacks. Otherwise, if the shack dwellers are deprived of shelter from the wind and rain as we approach the depths of autumn and winter, allowing them to live exposed to snow and frost would be contrary to humanity. If you could act as requested by the delegation, the entire association would be most grateful. We are writing to request that your department investigate and take appropriate action. This is addressed to the Director-General of the Public Works Department of the Shanghai Public Concession.

Dredging Bureau Iron Barge Obstructs Rice Boats 188

Two Rice Industry Groups in Northern Shanghai Petition for Prohibition

The Shanghai Northern Rice Merchants United Association and the Shanghai Rice Grain Industry Association jointly submitted a petition to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, stating: "We are submitting this petition to request action. According to reports from various members, the iron barges of the Dredging Bureau, which carry mud from dredging the river channels, are extremely large and do not tow barges. When the barges navigate the Wusong River to the outer port, the barges' hulls are huge, and when sailing, the wheels are not dragged behind the ship and are attached next to the wheel, occupying about half of the total river area. The captains neglect their duties, collide straight, and do not care about anything, causing damage to rice boats and other cargo ships. The Water Patrol Team of the Public Security Bureau can do nothing about it. We request that you forward this petition to the higher authorities, severely punish the boat captains, and negotiate with the Bureau to provide a guarantee that such incidents will not occur again. Otherwise, they should be responsible for compensating for the losses. After investigation, the damaged ships are listed as follows: 1. He Guirong's rice boat was hit in the bow, and the rice was wet, losing 21 shi. 2. Zhang Bingsheng's rice boat was hit with a hole on the west side of Hengfeng Bridge. 3. Yuan Si's rice boat was hit at Hengfeng Bridge, taking in water, and losing 20-30 shi of rice. 4. Xie Wenxiang's rice boat was damaged in the bow and stern shed east of Wuzhen Bridge. 5. Fei Zixiang's rice boat was damaged by wet rice. 6. Tang Zixiang's rice boat's cable dragon board was damaged. 7. Zhangsheng's rice boat's guardrail was damaged. 8. A lime boat was hit and sunk east of Wuzhen Bridge. 9. The guard pile on the west side of Wuzhen Bridge was broken. Because the water patrol teams could not interfere, the above-mentioned damaged rice boats had to endure in silence. The Wusong River channel is not wide, and it is an area where rice boats gather, as well as a passage for other merchant ships. Now that winter is approaching, the tide is gradually falling, and the river surface is even shallower. If we don't implement strict warnings and guarantees for the future, the resulting disasters will be unimaginable. Therefore, we specially report the situation and request the (Your Bureau)(Your Association) to quickly review and transfer the situation to the Dredging Bureau for negotiation. The boat captains should be punished and guaranteed to ensure that the above-mentioned situations do not occur again. Iron barges should tow wheels behind them and should not sail side by side again. Otherwise, they should be fully liable for compensation for damages. We also pray that you will forward this letter to the Public Security Bureau, ordering the Zhabei Water Patrol Team to provide effective protection. The Public Affairs Bureau Director Wu also sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Recent News on the Telephone Negotiations for the Extra-Boundary Road Construction 189

Slight Progress in Negotiations

Da Mei Evening News reports that the negotiations for the telephone contract for road construction beyond the boundary have reached the final stage, and the Public Concession authorities and the Shanghai Telephone Company are conducting negotiations independently. According to reliable sources, the Ministry of Communications has dispatched representatives to Shanghai to facilitate the early conclusion of the contract. The draft contract, which has been approved by the Shanghai Municipal Government, stipulates that in addition to paying 10,000 yuan annually, the company should pay the telephone bureau 12 yuan per telephone set per year as the price for obtaining the franchise in the Hongkou area. The company wants this 20 yuan to be borne by the users, but the Public Works Department, based on the telephone franchise contract, stipulates that user fees should be uniform and not discriminate. Considering that there are not many such telephone sets and that the company has great opportunities for development in the western area of Shanghai in the future, it insists that the company should bear the cost. The two sides have been discussing this back and forth for nearly two months. It is heard that there has been slight progress, and the telephone bureau may also be willing to make some concessions in exchange for other favorable conditions. It is expected that a new solution may be reported at the Public Works Department's review meeting on Thursday.

Seven Japanese Fishing Vessels Encountered Danger and Disappeared off Xiamen 190

Two Hundred Japanese People Are Missing

The Japanese Consul Requests Our Authorities to Assist in the Rescue

The Japanese Consulate has received a confirmed report that seven Japanese fishing vessels, which had invaded our country's South China Sea for fishing, encountered a sudden typhoon while fishing off the coast of Xiamen. Each vessel had more than two hundred Japanese fishermen, shipowners, and drivers, with about thirty people per ship. The seven vessels attempted to seek shelter in Xiamen harbor, but three days have passed since the typhoon subsided, and there is no trace of these seven vessels. It is feared that most of them have been lost, and the whereabouts of the more than two hundred Japanese people on board are also unknown. Yesterday, the Japanese Consulate notified various Japanese shipping companies in Shanghai to assist in the search and rescue and telegraphed the governments of Fujian and Guangdong provinces, requesting them to assist in the rescue efforts.

Post Office Investigates Newspaper Registration Certificates 195

Removal of Registered Benefits and Bonds for Those Who Do Not Submit Certificates for Investigation

It is learned that the postal authorities have stated that since the promulgation and implementation of the National Government's Publication Law this spring, all newspapers and magazines published in the country should, in accordance with Article 7 of this law and its implementation rules, be submitted to the provincial and municipal governments for transfer to the Ministry of Interior for verification and issuance of registration certificates for transfer to the post office for verification. Only then can they continue to enjoy the postal convenience. The bureau issued a circular to various newspapers for compliance after receiving orders on this matter last month. However, it was found that many of the newspapers, as many as three or four hundred, had not notified the post office of their relocation, or the houses had been renovated, or they had not returned from evacuation, and it was impossible to deliver the circular. After repeated visits and investigations, there were no results. None of these newspapers have taken the initiative to send this registration certificate for verification. Therefore, the bureau will report this situation to the Directorate General of Posts after waiting for a considerable period of time as a cancellation of registration and revocation of registration benefits, and there is no other way.

Public Hospital Specializes in the Treatment of Epidemic Throat Diseases 197

Purely Charitable in Nature

The Chinese Public Hospital on Qingyun Road and Tongji Road in Zhabei has treated countless patients with diphtheria, scarlet fever, and other diseases, and it has been trusted by Chinese and foreigners alike for many years. Unfortunately, during the January 28th Incident this year, the hospital was destroyed by artillery fire, and the buildings were reduced to ashes. The hospital's operations were suspended, and those suffering from throat diseases lost a savior. Director Chen Bingqian and others, in view of this, donated funds to rebuild the new building on the original site, which is brand new. Director Chen Weihan presides over the hospital's affairs, and the facilities are complete, and the hospital continues to provide consultations. Since the beginning of autumn, throat disease has become an epidemic. As soon as the hospital uses the latest treatment methods for injections, patients are brought back to life. Moreover, the hospital is purely charitable in nature, and the poor and sick are not charged. Those who lack the funds to return home after recovery are also given travel expenses by the hospital.

Sentenced to Twenty Years Imprisonment

Tang Bingchang, a native of Changzhou, gathered a gang on the morning of August 20th last year around 6 a.m. at the entrance of Shenxin No. 9 Cotton Mill on Yangshupu Road, and shot and wounded Zhao Xilin, a local who had previously served as a detective in the Changzhou Public Security Bureau, intending to take his life. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Zhen presided over the Third Criminal Court and sentenced Tang Bingchang to twenty years of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the final judgment shall be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days.

Child Scalded to Death by Boiling Water 201

The Riskshaw Puller is Hard to Avoid Blame

Li Zhangshen, an employee of the Senyuan Silk Factory in Panjiazhai, Xuxu Road, Shanghai, from Huzhou, has a son named Abao, who is four years old. As the only son and heir, he is doted on. Therefore, Li likes to keep him by his side. On the 4th of this month, Abao was playing by the roadside when Shen Sannv, a 13-year-old girl from the neighborhood, was passing by carrying boiling water. At the same time, Ding Yuncheng and Zhou Shoucheng, laborers dispatched by the Asia Petroleum Company, were pulling a rickshaw. Unexpectedly, their vehicle drove to the side of the road and knocked down Shen Sannv, causing a pot of boiling water to spill on Li Abao, scalding his abdomen and lower body. Li Zhangbao heard the news and rushed out, grabbing Ding and the others and taking them to the Second District Police Station. He also sent Abao to Guangci Hospital for treatment. However, the injuries were too severe, and he died the night before last. Yesterday, Li Zhangbao filed a complaint with the District Court, requesting an autopsy. Fire at Heiwa Yoko Wharf Yesterday Afternoon 207

The V-building warehouse on the fourth floor of Heiwa Yoko Wharf, No. 248 Qinhuangdao Road, Yangshupu, which stored about 500 bales of cotton, caught fire yesterday afternoon around 2 PM due to a cigarette butt igniting a bale of cotton. Suddenly, black smoke billowed and flames shot out. The wharf supervisor noticed it and immediately called the Yangshupu Fire Brigade, which rushed to the scene to extinguish the fire with all their might. It took more than an hour to put out the fire. An estimated one hundred bales of cotton were burned or damaged by water. Fortunately, the fire did not spread to the building, which can be said to be a great stroke of luck in the midst of misfortune.

Pudong Gaoqiao Police Chief's Illegal Abuse of Power Case 208

Closing Arguments Concluded, Awaiting Sentencing

Zheng 　, the police chief of the Fourth Sub-bureau of the Third District (Gaoqiao, Pudong) of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, was recently accused by Chen Chen and other people from the village to the Shanghai District Court Procuratorate of accepting bribes and abusing his power illegally. The prosecutor investigated and determined the facts, and filed a lawsuit with the Criminal Court, requesting a public trial. The public trial was held a few days ago and was not concluded. It is now known that Zheng 　 hired Xu Heling and Wang Jian, two lawyers, to submit a defense to the Criminal Court, which can be divided into three points: ㈠ The part of the accusation of illegally punishing the monk Zhao was that on March 23rd of this year, a police officer was dispatched to patrol the countryside and learned that Zhao Dongdong's teahouse in Lingjia Wood Bridge was recruiting people to gamble. The police went to arrest them, but Zhao Heshang tipped them off, so they were not caught. Zhao was taken to the station and fined five yuan in accordance with the Prohibition and Penalty Law, as a warning, because there was gambling in the teahouse and Zhao tipped off the violators, causing them to escape. This was an administrative penalty. The police chief immediately reported to the Public Security Bureau and posted a monthly notice to inform the public. Obviously, there was no direct or indirect intention to profit, and there was no crime to speak of. The report to the Public Security Bureau also did not have any refuting instructions. The appropriateness of the punishment is undeniable, and the appropriate punishment cannot be regarded as a criminal act. The original indictment stated that he should be guilty of Article 136 of the Criminal Law, which is a misunderstanding. ㈡ The part of the accusation of illegal detention and extortion of Sun Zhangqi was that on May 10th of this year, Shen Zhangqi (that is, Sun Zhangqi) went to claim the boat with Liu Liantao and used intimidating means to forcibly demand it from Xin Zhanggen, the pond chief, and Xu Bingbing. Xin Zhanggen and Xu Bingbing brought Shen Zhangqi and Liu Liantao to the station. According to the confession, there were many discrepancies, and the license plate number could not be specified. They only claimed that the boat was rented from someone else and were ordered to submit a lease, which was delayed for several days and never submitted. Obviously, they were fraudulently claiming it, so they were submitted to the Public Security Bureau for verification on the 15th. It has been several months since then, and there is still no record of a claim. The temporary custody cannot be considered an abuse of detention. The original indictment, based on Sun Zhangqi's one-sided confession, stated that he was illegally detained for eight days and should be guilty of Article 140 and Article 316, paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, which is extremely unjust. ㈢ The part of the accusation of accepting bribes from Gu Amao, Huang Jinchu, and Gao Linquan was that on March 17th of this year, the Public Security Bureau ordered an investigation into the case of Zheng Zhulin and others suing Gao Linquan and others for jointly robbing property. The patrol officer was immediately ordered to investigate secretly, but it was not the case. For the sake of caution, the police chief ordered Gu, Huang, and Gao to obtain a proper guarantee and wait for a summons. There are also guarantors Zhong Yulin, Lu Shaofeng, and Chen Xueqing who can be interrogated. Whether the police chief accepted bribes will be clear after an interrogation. However, according to the confession of Gu Amao and others in the file, a total of 200 yuan was paid. Gu Amao and Huang Jinchu each paid 67 yuan, and Gao Linquan paid 66 yuan, which Chen Jinxiu paid on their behalf. Whether this confession is true is said to be in violation of Article 129, paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law, which seems arbitrary. He requested a judgment of innocence. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Guan Liting continued the trial. Zheng 　 and lawyers Xu and Wang arrived in court and stated the previous situation. Then, Chen Jinxiu testified, "I guaranteed Gu Amao, but I don't know if Gu paid money." The judge ordered Gu Amao to confront him. Gu confessed that he did give Chen Jinxiu 200 yuan. The judge asked if there was any evidence, and he replied no. Then, Chen Chen and other witnesses testified. The judge ordered the start of closing arguments. Lawyers Xu Heling and Wang Jian then rose to defend for a long time. The judge ordered the closing arguments to be concluded and set the sentencing for 2 PM on the 11th of this month.

Weng Afu Commits Assault and Injury 209

Sentenced to One Year and Six Months

Weng Afu, a Ningbo native residing at No. 506 Siwenli, Dalianwan Road, colluded with Deng Youwen (his nephew), who is at large, at 7:30 PM the day before yesterday to seek revenge on Shen Changyuan, a fellow villager at No. 3 Xiang'anli, Dongxihuade Road. They fought each other and used a kitchen knife to cut Shen's left index finger, causing him to bleed profusely and fall to the ground crying for help. Chinese detective Zhao Ruisheng heard the alarm and arrived to arrest Weng and brought him and the murder weapon to the Huishan Police Station. The head of the police ordered him to be detained. The police also sent the injured person to the hospital for treatment. Yesterday morning, the police sent the prisoner Weng to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the previous situation and stated that the cause of the case was that the plaintiff Shen Changyuan's brother-in-law Wang Atong had a relationship with the defendant's nephew Deng Youwen's sister. Yesterday, Deng and the defendant went to quarrel, angered Shen Changyuan, and had a dispute. He then used a kitchen knife to cut Shen's finger. After the doctor's inspection, the index finger has been severed. Now, the victim and witness Wei Wushi have both arrived in court to testify and requested a severe punishment. Detective Zhao then reported the details of the case and presented the kitchen knife for inspection. According to the victim Shen Changyuan's complaint, he had never met the defendant before. The plaintiff's brother-in-law Wang Atong and the defendant's nephew Deng Youwen had a dispute over renting a room. Yesterday, they came to cause trouble and make a fuss. He mediated the dispute. The defendant loudly said that it would be okay to kill him. There were a total of four people on the defendant's side, each holding iron rods and sharp blades. As a result, he was cut off his index finger with a knife. The woman Wei Wushi testified that she lived with the plaintiff and that she saw the defendant cut the plaintiff's finger with a knife. Weng Afu's confession was evasive. After Judge Shen Bingrong verified the confession, he ordered the court clerk to take Shen Changyuan to the forensic doctor's office for an examination. He then sentenced Weng Afu to one year and six months of imprisonment and confiscated the murder weapon.

Two Dismissed Chinese Detectives Impersonate Officers and Extort Money 211

Sentenced to 40 Days of Detention Each

Guo Wenbin from Tianjin and Sun Guimao from Funing, two dismissed Chinese detectives, together with an accomplice, went to the home of Xu Binglian, a Jiangbei native who ran a shoe business at No. 28 Dapu Lane, Jin Shenfu Road, in the French Concession on the evening of the 6th at 11 PM. Guo impersonated Zhou Ruiyuan, a detective from the French Concession, and Sun impersonated Bao Detective Wang Fusheng. They entered the house on the pretext of arresting people for running a lottery. They saw Xu and his friends Huang Fuyuan, Yin Yuyuan, and Ye Qingxiang playing mahjong at a table, and searched each of them, finding a total of 79 yuan in cash, banknotes, and small change, which they hid on their bodies. They also ransacked the boxes and cabinets, and took Xu out of the house on the pretext of taking him to the police station. When they arrived at the intersection of Sapo Sai Road, they released Xu. Guo and others then fled in different directions and divided the spoils. The police were notified and arrested Guo and Sun on Caishi Road the next evening. They found a wallet on Guo's body, which still contained stolen money, as well as pawn tickets for clothes and other items. They were taken to the police station and sent to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special Court yesterday for investigation. First, the police lawyer Chen Ming stated the facts of the case and filed a lawsuit in accordance with Articles 166 and 337 of the Criminal Law. Then, the plaintiff Xu Binglian stated that the defendants impersonated detectives and went to his home, and seized silver dollars from everyone on the pretext of arresting people for running a lottery. The witnesses Huang Fuyuan, Yin Yuyuan, and Ye Qingxiang also testified in court, proving everything. When questioned, the two defendants categorically denied impersonating detectives and extorting money, and claimed that they were being framed out of malice. Judge Xiong verified the confession and stated that the case had been proven and could not be denied. He then sentenced Guo Wenbin and Sun Guimao to 40 days of detention each for the crime of joint intimidation and ordered the stolen money to be returned to the owner.

Theft Case Cracked in the Seventh District 212

The home of Tan Chengshi, a widow residing in Tanjiazhai, Beishou, Wusong, was suddenly visited by seven bandits with painted faces on the evening before last at 11 PM. Each held a weapon and broke down the door, rushing straight into the inner room. Tan Chengshi and her daughter A Bao were awakened from their dreams. Because there were only mother and daughter in the house, they were locked in the room by the bandits. The bandits then searched at will for about half an hour. As a result, they were robbed of 75 silver dollars and three large packages of clothing and accessories. Because A Bao was getting married soon, the clothing and accessories were all newly made. After the bandits had looted their fill, they each carried the stolen goods out the door and fled west. Yesterday morning, the local bailiff Tan Songxing reported to the Seventh District Public Security Bureau and requested an arrest. After District Chief Li Jing received the report, he immediately sent district officials to investigate with police detectives. They determined that Ni Erlang, the male servant of the house, was suspicious, and took Ni to the district office for questioning. Ni claimed that he was not involved in the case, but that he knew about the bandits' plan in advance. He then confessed that the case was committed by Chu Jinsheng, Gu Axiao, Cao Gengen, Wang Heshang, and four others. After District Chief Li received the confession, he sent district officials Yin Gongtian, patrol officers Yang Xihui and Zeng Shufan, and detectives Wang Yao and Gu Yousan to secretly arrest them at their addresses. They learned that the bandits Cao Gengen and Gu Axiao were hiding in a thatch shed near Daxing'an Bridge, and they rushed in and arrested the two bandits, who did not resist. They then arrested the bandit leader Chu Jinsheng on Guizhi Road in Wusong Town, and brought them all to the district office for questioning. The three bandits all confessed to the joint robbery. District Chief Li ordered them to be detained and ordered the arrest of the four bandits who were at large for severe punishment.

Autumn Champagne Ticket Numbers of the Race Club Announced 213

The Shanghai Race Club Members' Club issues member champagne tickets every spring and autumn. This year, although it issued one-eighth more, all 12,500 tickets were sold out half a month ago, truly an unprecedented new record. The drawing of the champagne tickets is based entirely on the Shanghai Race Club's Grand Champagne Race. The number of winning numbers depends on the number of horses that pass the preliminary round. This year, there were 38 horses that passed the preliminary round, plus 5 reserve horses today (Champagne is the sixth race), for a total of 43 horses. Therefore, there were 43 winning numbers. It was originally scheduled to be held at the club's new clubhouse, but because of construction issues, it was not completed. Therefore, it was specially borrowed from the Shanghai Race Club drawing room, as scheduled at 8 PM yesterday. Under the supervision of the guests Lang Jingshan and Zhou Fuqi, and the execution of the club's board of directors, the drawing was held in public. As for who the first, second, and third prizes belong to, it depends on the results of today's horse race. The East Asia Daily was searched by the police two days ago, and reporter Zhang Lin was arrested. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Second Branch of the High Court. The trial began at 11 AM. Special Delivery

Judge Feetham's Report on the Shanghai International Settlement, Volume IV (17), Appendix 43 228

Regulations Regarding the Conduct of Councillors Contained in the Durban Municipal Ordinance Durban Local Government Ordinance of 1926 (Sections 38 to 43)

Section 38. A Councillor or His Partner, Employer, or Employee Shall Not Undertake Specialized Business to Represent or Oppose the Municipal Council for Remuneration

(1) No Municipal Councillor, or his partner, or his employer, or employee, shall, for remuneration, undertake the business of advocate, solicitor, notary public, conveyancer, or litigation agent to represent or oppose the Municipal Council, and no Municipal Councillor, or his partner, or his employer, or employee, shall, for remuneration, undertake the business of medical practitioner, veterinary surgeon, engineer, surveyor, auctioneer, appraiser, or valuer, or any other specialized business to represent the Municipal Council, but (a) the remuneration paid to any medical practitioner as required by law, ordinance, or bylaw for issuing a certificate regarding any infectious disease on behalf of the Municipal Council shall not apply to the provisions of this section, (b) if a medical practitioner is requested by two-thirds of the Municipal Councillors to represent the Municipal Council and obtains the permission of the Governor-General, the medical practitioner may represent the Municipal Council, (c) if at the time of the commencement of this Ordinance there is any agreement whereby any employer of a Municipal Councillor may perform specialized business on behalf of the Municipal Council, such arrangement may continue until the term for which the Municipal Councillor was elected under any law repealed by this Ordinance or under the Municipal Elections Ordinance of 1912 and any amendment thereof expires.

(2) Any Municipal Councillor who is convicted of violating the provisions of this section shall be fined a maximum of fifty pounds. The court that convicts the Municipal Councillor may order the Municipal Councillor to return the remuneration received for performing the aforementioned matters and remove him from his position as Municipal Councillor, without replacement.

Section 39. Regulations Regarding a Municipal Councillor's Contractual Relationship with the Municipal Council

(1) The provisions of this section shall apply to the Municipal Councils of the cities listed in the Third Schedule of this Ordinance, and to other Municipal Councils designated by the Governor-General in a notice in the Provincial Gazette from time to time.

(2) No Municipal Councillor shall, on behalf of himself, or on behalf of his wife, or on behalf of a company related to himself or his wife, enter into a contract with the Municipal Council, to have any work performed, or to act as a vendor or purchaser, etc., by the Municipal Council, or the Municipal Councillor, or the company. Any contract or transaction agreement entered into with the Municipal Council, or on behalf of the Municipal Council, to which the Municipal Councillor has a direct or indirect relationship, shall be deemed invalid. Any subcontract or transaction agreement entered into by any Municipal Councillor, or to which any Municipal Councillor has a direct or indirect relationship, based on any contract entered into by the Municipal Council, for the purpose of performing work, supplying goods, or transferring property, shall also be deemed invalid. However, any contract or transaction agreement shall not be deemed invalid or repealed pursuant to the provisions of this section if the Municipal Councillor's only relationship is that he has invested capital in a company, or if the contract is entered into by the Municipal Council to supply any items or conduct any affairs, and the fees charged are calculated according to commonly published prices, or if the Municipal Councillor purchases real estate or goods at a public auction held by the Municipal Council.

(3) Any Municipal Councillor who is convicted of violating the provisions of this section shall be fined a maximum of fifty pounds, and if not paid, shall be imprisoned for a maximum of three months with or without hard labor. The court that convicts the Municipal Councillor may order him to report to the Municipal Council all the benefits obtained from entering into the contract or transaction agreement, and remove him from his position as Municipal Councillor, without replacement.

(2) Except for the provisions of Section 38 of this Ordinance, Section 6 of the Municipal Elections Ordinance of 1912 (as amended by Section 1 of Ordinance No. 13 of 1925) (Note), and Section 125 of this Ordinance, no Municipal Councillor shall be prohibited from entering into a contract with the Municipal Council as a seller, purchaser, or otherwise, by reason of his position. Any contract or transaction agreement entered into with the Municipal Council, or on behalf of the Municipal Council, or any subcontract or subsequently entered into transaction agreement formed under any such contract, shall not be deemed invalid or repealed by reason of a direct or indirect relationship with any Municipal Councillor. Any Municipal Councillor who enters into a contract or has such a relationship shall not be required to report to the Municipal Council any benefits derived from entering into such contract or transaction agreement by reason of his position or the fiduciary relationship arising from his being a Councillor, except as provided below in this section.

(3) Any Municipal Councillor who is not a shareholder of a limited liability company and who has a relationship with any contract or transaction agreement entered into with the Municipal Council, or with any subcontract or subsequently entered into transaction agreement formed under such contract or transaction agreement, and who, in accordance with the provisions of such contract or transaction agreement, is required to be paid or receive one hundred pounds or more from the Municipal Council, shall declare his relationship to the Municipal Council before the Municipal Council convenes to decide or approve such contract or transaction agreement, or at the time of the meeting. If the relationship arises at the time when the Municipal Council decides or approves such contract, or after the decision or approval, it shall be declared to the Municipal Council within a reasonable period of time, no later than one month after the occurrence of such relationship. If the declaration is not made at a meeting of the Municipal Council, the relationship may be communicated to the Municipal Secretary in writing, who shall then report it at the first Council meeting after receiving the letter. Any such declaration shall be recorded in the minutes of the Municipal Council meeting at which the Municipal Councillor makes the declaration or at which the Municipal Secretary reports it. However, any such relationship need not be declared in any of the following circumstances:

(a) Where the Municipal Council has expressly permitted the Municipal Councillor to enter into any contract or transaction agreement in his own name.

(b) Where the Municipal Council has expressly permitted a contract or transaction agreement entered into with any merchant or company, and the Municipal Councillor has, after being most recently appointed as a Municipal Councillor, notified the Municipal Secretary in writing of any relationship with such merchant or company.

(4) Any Municipal Councillor who is found to have failed to declare any relationship with any contract or transaction agreement entered into with the Municipal Council, or with any subcontract or subsequently entered into transaction agreement, in accordance with the provisions of this section, shall be fined a maximum of fifty pounds, and if not paid, shall be imprisoned for a maximum of three months with or without hard labor. The court that convicts the Municipal Councillor may order him to report to the Municipal Council all the benefits obtained from entering into the contract or transaction agreement, and remove him from his position as Municipal Councillor, without replacement. However, if it is proven that any Municipal Councillor's failure to declare such a relationship was due to illness, absence from his city, error, negligence, or other similar cause, and not due to any lack of integrity, the court shall not issue such an order.

(5) Each month, the Municipal Treasurer, or in the absence of a Municipal Treasurer, the Municipal Secretary, shall, based on the most accurate information available to him, compile a statement listing any contract or transaction agreement entered into or approved by the Municipal Council in the past month that has a relationship with any Municipal Councillor, other than as a shareholder of a limited liability company. The names of the Municipal Councillors with such relationships shall also be stated. This statement shall be submitted to the Municipal Council at the first Municipal Council meeting after its completion, and the statement shall be recorded in the minutes of the meeting.

(6) The auditor appointed by the Governor-General to audit the accounts of the Municipal Council shall, from time to time, review the books of the Municipal Council to determine whether the provisions of this section have been complied with. If any non-compliance is found, it shall be reported to the Governor-General. (To be continued)
